  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_01051d51-a22c-4ec1-8345-459c9ea013a0'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer2552975271144305149">Landover was a genuine magic kingdom, complete with fairy folk and wizardry, just as the advertisement had promised.   <span id="freeText2552975271144305149" style="display:none">Landover was a genuine magic kingdom, complete with fairy folk and wizardry, just as the advertisement had promised. But after he purchased it for a million dollars, Ben Holiday discovered that there were a few details the ad had failed to mention. Such as the fact that the kingdom was falling into ruin. The barons refused to recognize a king and taxes hadn't been collected for years. The dragon, Strabo, was laying waste to the countryside, while the evil witch, Nightshade, was plotting to destroy no less than everything. And if that weren't enough for a prospective king to deal with, Ben soon learned that the Iron Mark, terrible lord of the demons, challenged all pretenders to the throne of Landover to a duel to the death - a duel no mere mortal could hope to win. But Ben Holiday had one human trait that even magic couldn't overcome. Ben Holiday was stubborn.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">There are no overly adult themes in the book. Love, loss, and combat are all handled pretty lightly without a lot of over the top or in depth detail. <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">There are no overly adult themes in the book. Love, loss, and combat are all handled pretty lightly without a lot of over the top or in depth detail. This should be fine for any teenage or adult reader.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

    <a title="Patrick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/922495-patrick"><img alt="Patrick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351307095p2/922495.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2065981495?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/922495-patrick">Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2065981495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17923652871975129200">I saw this in a used bookstore and picked it up as a nostaglia re-read.<br/><br/>It's a good book, and I enjoyed it. But the pace of the story is much *much* slower than I remember. Part of this might be that I already had read it in the past. Or that I'm much *much* busier than I was as a kid. <br/><br/>But the result is that I ended up doing something I rarely do: I skimmed chunks of the book, mostly description or narration of the main character's thoughts, so I could get to the next bit of action or dialogue.<br/><br/>Fo</span>
  <span id="freeText17923652871975129200" style="display:none">I saw this in a used bookstore and picked it up as a nostaglia re-read.<br /><br />It's a good book, and I enjoyed it. But the pace of the story is much *much* slower than I remember. Part of this might be that I already had read it in the past. Or that I'm much *much* busier than I was as a kid. <br /><br />But the result is that I ended up doing something I rarely do: I skimmed chunks of the book, mostly description or narration of the main character's thoughts, so I could get to the next bit of action or dialogue.<br /><br />For all that, I think it held up pretty well. But I don't know if I'm excited enough to dig up a copy of the sequel and dive right in....</span>
  <a data-text-id="17923652871975129200" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1826561-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1414300337p2/1826561.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/43827510?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/1826561-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1826561-laura?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer43827510" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13787092840108338530">This was a book that constantly frustrated me by not making the most of its premise. Here you have a pretty original premise, a humorous tone, and a diverse cast of characters, and yet all that emerges is a mildly engaging but not wholly entertaining read. There were countless missed opportunities, and I couldn't help wondering how this book would have fared in, say, Terry Pratchett's far more capable hands.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_18099052" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18099052" />
    <a title="Werner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/903390-werner"><img alt="Werner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1216337931p2/903390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18099052?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Werner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Werner" href="/user/show/903390-werner">Werner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of fantasy with a humorous touch</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/903390-werner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/903390-werner?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18099052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15566249455186788646">My wife Barb enjoys being read to (as well as reading by herself), and generally likes fantasy, as do I. So it's not surprising that we've read a fair amount together in that genre, nor that Terry Brooks was an author we ran across early. We first read and liked his debut novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15575.The_Sword_of_Shannara__The_Original_Shannara_Trilogy___1_' title='The Sword of Shannara (The Original Shannara Trilogy, #1) by Terry Brooks' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Sword of Shannara</a>, reasonably well; but we both agree that it has a very derivative dependence on Tolkien, which goes far beyond the obvious influence the British genre giant exerted on all the fantasists who followe</span>
  <span id="freeText15566249455186788646" style="display:none">My wife Barb enjoys being read to (as well as reading by herself), and generally likes fantasy, as do I. So it's not surprising that we've read a fair amount together in that genre, nor that Terry Brooks was an author we ran across early. We first read and liked his debut novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15575.The_Sword_of_Shannara__The_Original_Shannara_Trilogy___1_" title="The Sword of Shannara (The Original Shannara Trilogy, #1) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sword of Shannara</a>, reasonably well; but we both agree that it has a very derivative dependence on Tolkien, which goes far beyond the obvious influence the British genre giant exerted on all the fantasists who followed him. (In fairness to Brooks, he does display more originality in at least a couple of the voluminous Shannara sequels, though those are the only ones we've read.) The Magic Kingdom of Landover series (of which this novel is the opener), IMO, is where Brooks actually finds his own authentic voice, and produces something that's not just a Tolkien knock-off. For that reason, and because of its intrinsic appeal, it's the part of his corpus that we've liked the best and returned to the most.<br /><br />I've characterized this as "fantasy with a humorous touch," not "humorous fantasy." By that distinction, I mean that it's not written with the sole purpose of being funny practically from cover to cover, in the manner of, say, Terry Pratchett's Discworld books or Robert Asprin's Myth Conceptions series. Our protagonist has experienced tragedy and been marked by it, which sets up the whole premise here; the situation and plotting is not inherently humorous, and involves real danger, and Brooks incorporates serious (and constructive) psychological messages woven into the warp and woof of the tale. But he also leavens it with a certain strand of situational and verbal humor in places (the character of Questor Thews in particular helps to provide comic relief at times, as do the antics of the G'home Gnomes --so called because any people they visit soon come to tell them "Go home, Gnomes!"-- though I can't remember if they're actually introduced in this book). The overall tone is also, to my mind, somewhat lighter than that of the Shannara books that I've read.<br /><br />Though only 39, Ben Holiday is a very successful --and as a result, very wealthy; lawyers in his milieu can make a LOT of money-- corporate attorney. But since the accidental death of his pregnant wife two years ago, he's been empty inside, just going through the motions of living, ready for an escape --any escape. So when, as our story opens, his fortuitous thumbing through a high-priced gift catalog turns up an ad for a supposedly <i>bona fide</i> kingship of a land where magic genuinely works, dragons exist, and medieval chivalry prevails, for the price of a million dollars, he's actually ready to consider the invitation "Escape into your dreams and be born again." Of course, he thinks, it has to be a bogus come-on. As it turns out, it's not. Landover really exists, in a dimension of reality apart from our world but accessible, if you know how to do it; and a mysterious man named Meeks will truly peddle that knowledge, for the asking price. But there are a few critical facts that the ad doesn't mention, and which our hero will learn only once he's in Landover....<br /><br />Brooks tells a good, involving story, well-paced, with rounded and engaging characters whom the reader will like (well, except for the villains). Fantasy elements are handled effectively, and will appeal to genre fans. While it's not written with younger readers directly in mind, the book is suitable for all ages; I don't recall any noticeable bad language, there's no sexual content, and none of the violence is grisly-gory. The sociology of Landover (beyond the fact that its human society is feudal, with barons ruling over peasants) isn't particularly well developed, and Ben's journey towards emotional healing is arguably a bit too glib, and not treated with great psychological depth. But those are relatively minor quibbles.<br /><br />There are six books in the series to date; Barb and I read and liked the next four: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/92845.The_Black_Unicorn__Magic_Kingdom_of_Landover___2_" title="The Black Unicorn (Magic Kingdom of Landover, #2) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">The Black Unicorn</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15561.Wizard_at_Large__Magic_Kingdom_of_Landover__3_" title="Wizard at Large (Magic Kingdom of Landover #3) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Wizard at Large</a>; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34942.The_Tangle_Box__Magic_Kingdom_of_Landover___4_" title="The Tangle Box (Magic Kingdom of Landover, #4) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">The Tangle Box</a>; and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15564.Witches__Brew__Magic_Kingdom_of_Landover___5_" title="Witches' Brew (Magic Kingdom of Landover, #5) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Witches' Brew</a>. All of these were read back in the 90s, and we got the books at a local flea market. I only became aware of the sixth book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6202861.A_Princess_of_Landover__Magic_Kingdom_of_Landover___6_" title="A Princess of Landover (Magic Kingdom of Landover, #6) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">A Princess of Landover</a>, very recently, so I can't say anything about it specifically. But (since, knowing how much of a backlog of retrospective reviews of pre-Goodreads books I need to write, I'm unlikely to review the others individually) I will say I'd recommend all of the first five books to fantasy fans, and to those wanting to try out the genre. (The books really should be read in order, to better understand the characters and story arc.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="15566249455186788646" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1618895211" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1618895211" />
    <a title="A. Dawes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55066255-a-dawes"><img alt="A. Dawes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470731545p2/55066255.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1618895211?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="A. Dawes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="A. Dawes" href="/user/show/55066255-a-dawes">A. Dawes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1618895211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14235356690386878587">This is lighter fare - the kind of book that takes your mind off the real world. Having read it almost three decades ago, I don't know if I'm truly qualified to review it now, but I remember it as a refreshing palate cleanser at the time. I went on to read and enjoy three more in the series. <br/><br/>Plot wise, it's not overly original. It's the basic portal Narnia type of novel. So I can't say that it shaped the field or massively influenced it. Basically, your white American male, Ben Holiday, is a lit</span>
  <span id="freeText14235356690386878587" style="display:none">This is lighter fare - the kind of book that takes your mind off the real world. Having read it almost three decades ago, I don't know if I'm truly qualified to review it now, but I remember it as a refreshing palate cleanser at the time. I went on to read and enjoy three more in the series. <br /><br />Plot wise, it's not overly original. It's the basic portal Narnia type of novel. So I can't say that it shaped the field or massively influenced it. Basically, your white American male, Ben Holiday, is a little over the mundane American lifestyle and purchases the Magical Kingdom of Landover for $1 million dollars. Landover is the real McCoy, replete with wizards and all manner of fae folk. It seems the perfect opportunity to start afresh for Ben.<br /><br />Yet, like any bargain, there's a catch. The Kingdom has been neglected: greedy barons haven't paid taxes; there's a dragon called Strabo wreaking havoc on the farmlands; a nefarious witch, Nightshade, who takes pleasure in destruction; and finally, the Lord of the Demonic Underworld has challenged the new king, Ben, to a duel to the death. <br /><br />But Ben has friends, a wizard who Ben has turned into a talking dog, and a dryad-like lady who transforms into a tree at night once a month. <br /><br />As you can imagine, it's simply a fun page turner. Brooks, as always, is fairly derivative, but he handles this world very well. And I'm eventually going to finish the rest of the series as it's simply a great escape.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14235356690386878587" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26552179" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12139325729534341029">It took me a while to sink into this book... seemed like a lot of time was spent in Ben Holiday's disbelief at finding himself in Landover. Yes, it was any sane person's natural response to leave town and enter a hidden world where a person can be accidentally half-transformed into a dog; I just don't want to spend so long wallowing in it. <br/><br/>It took me a while to feel any sort of sympathy for any of the characters. For most of the book I was laughing when they got into trouble - although some of t</span>
  <span id="freeText12139325729534341029" style="display:none">It took me a while to sink into this book... seemed like a lot of time was spent in Ben Holiday's disbelief at finding himself in Landover. Yes, it was any sane person's natural response to leave town and enter a hidden world where a person can be accidentally half-transformed into a dog; I just don't want to spend so long wallowing in it. <br /><br />It took me a while to feel any sort of sympathy for any of the characters. For most of the book I was laughing when they got into trouble - although some of the characters warrant it (particularly the inept wizard Questor, my favorite character). Not until Ben's harrowing journey through Fairie did I start caring about him at all.<br /><br />The women of the story were flat. While Willow was throwing herself at Ben I just gagged - although I liked her a little better when she turned out to be not quite the sex object Ben would have liked. And it was redeeming on Ben's part that threatened with her loss, he finally comes to accept her for what she is. Nightshade was more interesting, as the villains often are, but she was pretty much just evil, no motivation. Not that the male characters were particularly better, but at least they were original.<br /><br />The Paladin's secret was frankly cheesy, and I didn't feel there was really enough precedent for it. I may have just missed that, though. And the attempt to bring some sort of psychological depth to the story came off as a little less than poignant.<br /><br />Still, there were redeeming points and even a few deep thoughts. What do we seek in fantacy, be it through fiction or fairy tales, or through an ad in a department store wishbook? Is it for us as it is Ben Holiday - escape, wonder, nicely drawn lines between good and evil, big clashing battles instead of endless legalistic hearings in the name of justice? In the piece of anti-fantasy fantasy I'm cobbling together, I take lots of stabs at those things. But offered a chance to make a difference as a single person, I must admit I'd be sold.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12139325729534341029" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_942690112" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/942690112" />
    <a title="Nicole Pramik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24437209-nicole-pramik"><img alt="Nicole Pramik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442948364p2/24437209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/942690112?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole Pramik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole Pramik" href="/user/show/24437209-nicole-pramik">Nicole Pramik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24437209-nicole-pramik?shelf=books-reviewed">books-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24437209-nicole-pramik?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer942690112" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16456759599147730173"><i>Magic Kingdom for Sale – Sold!</i> is an enjoyable read. It isn’t epic like <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> but it’s not trying to be. Its world building is solid and believable and its characters are fun. Ben Holiday makes for a great, relatable protagonist with just enough flaws to keep him from being too perfect yet noble enough to keep him honorable. The secondary characters like Questor Thews (the court magician), Abernathy (the court scribe who was transformed into a dog), and Willow (the sylph), are in</span>
  <span id="freeText16456759599147730173" style="display:none"><i>Magic Kingdom for Sale – Sold!</i> is an enjoyable read. It isn’t epic like <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> but it’s not trying to be. Its world building is solid and believable and its characters are fun. Ben Holiday makes for a great, relatable protagonist with just enough flaws to keep him from being too perfect yet noble enough to keep him honorable. The secondary characters like Questor Thews (the court magician), Abernathy (the court scribe who was transformed into a dog), and Willow (the sylph), are interesting though they definitely fulfill some of the typical hero’s journey tropes (e.g. the wise old man, the comedic relief, the beautiful maiden, etc.). But Brooks can get away with that in this novel since it reads like a quasi-fairy tale, so having symbolic characters is okay.<br /><br />While the plot has a few slow parts, the majority of the story is well-hinged and kept me invested. The friendships Ben makes are organic and two characters’ romance is sweet and innocent without being cloying. Another big plus for me was that the villains avoided being too cartoony, with Nightshade being the most interesting of the darker figures and I can definitely see her becoming a thorn in Ben’s side in the series’ other novels. My only issue is that I thought Ben was a bit too forgiving towards another character considering the gravity of the other person’s offense. But, overall, I found very few flaws with this book.<br /><br />Lastly, the underlying messages of believing in the impossible and seeking to be set free from the fetters of the past and deep-seated fears were well executed. Where it would have been tempting for Brooks to preach, he instead weaves a slow thread that presents a satisfying conclusion yet leaves the door open for the series’ sequels. I finished this book eager to read more about Ben’s adventures and I will certainly try to get my hands on the other books in the series. (To date, I've read books two and three with an intent to finish the series at some point in the future.)<br /><br />Concerning content, Ben’s law partner likes to spout some choice PG and PG-13-level words but he’s not a main character except for some early chapters. Likewise, Ben sometimes makes profane exclamations in times of surprise or stress but these aren’t pervasive. Violence is minimal and while there are scenes of peril, these are free from overt violence and gore. Elsewhere, most of the violence is typical fantasy-style violence that involves magic and sword play with no graphic killings or tortures. Lastly, there is no sexual content. Ben undresses to bathe in a stream and sees Willow, naked (at a distance), standing in the water. This is a scene of pure innocence, so nothing is described in graphic detail and nothing sexual occurs between them in this scene or elsewhere in the novel. <br /><br />Overall, <i>Magic Kingdom for Sale – Sold!</i> is a fun, enjoyable read. Think of this novel as a bowl of creamy macaroni and cheese – cozy, enjoyable, and fulfilling. It may not break new ground in its genre but it’s honestly a likable book. Thus, if the <i>Shannara</i> series scares you due to its expansive size, give this novel (or series) a try as a good introduction to Brooks as a story teller and world builder. You won’t be disappointed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16456759599147730173" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_369717157" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/369717157" />
    <a title="Gemma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3987226-gemma"><img alt="Gemma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1279487231p2/3987226.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/369717157?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gemma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gemma" href="/user/show/3987226-gemma">Gemma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3987226-gemma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer369717157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2549742902551136960">I was intrigued by the premise of buying a fairy world (kingship included!), and thank God I was, because it took a few chapters for this to take off for me. Once things got settled, this was a pretty fun and entertaining read for me.<br/><br/>Ben Holiday, lawyer and widower, came across as mopey and unbalanced at first. I can't say he didn't have his reasons, though. His wife was dead, and he was contemplating buying the kingdom of Landover for one million dollars, all on a whim. He was full of doubts fo</span>
  <span id="freeText2549742902551136960" style="display:none">I was intrigued by the premise of buying a fairy world (kingship included!), and thank God I was, because it took a few chapters for this to take off for me. Once things got settled, this was a pretty fun and entertaining read for me.<br /><br />Ben Holiday, lawyer and widower, came across as mopey and unbalanced at first. I can't say he didn't have his reasons, though. His wife was dead, and he was contemplating buying the kingdom of Landover for one million dollars, all on a whim. He was full of doubts for being a successful thirty-something, but given the situation that seemed logical. Within ten minutes of setting foot in Landover, he had to escape the demon known as the Iron Mark and the dragon called Strabo, then ran across the would-be wizard Questor Thews, who wasted no time in demonstrating his ineptitude. Good start! I like how whenever Ben was in over his head trying to validate his claim to the throne, he fell back on his courtroom experience and stayed cool. It was training that served him well.<br /><br />It's hard to say who I liked best out of the secondary characters. Questor was well-meaning, Abernathy the talking dog (who was once human) was often sarcastic, but he had a level head and gave some good advice, even if Ben didn't take it. Willow the sylph wasn't a main player until about halfway through the book, but she was so steady I couldn't help but come to like her.<br /><br />There's problems in Landover, and that's for sure. The magic that keeps the land alive is failing, and the only way to save it is for a King to establish himself. But first Ben has to win over the people he'd be king to, and that's not going to be easy. Before the Lords of the Greensward will pledge to him, they want him to get rid of Strabo. Before the River Master will pledge to him, he wants Ben to stop the humans from polluting the river system. To get rid of Strabo, he'll have to convince the witch Nightshade to help him (and I doubt we've seen the last of her yet!). To top it all off, the Iron Mark has challenged him to a duel, and the only way he could possibly survive that is through the help of the Paladin, the King's protector and champion of old. Just one problem: no one has seen the Paladin in twenty years.<br /><br />If it weren't for the occasional swearing, I wouldn't have been able to guess that this was aimed at adults. It didn't take itself too seriously and it was at times light-hearted and, well, just plain fun. I also appreciated the old school fantasy characters as opposed to the generic ones we're stuck with today, and I can only hope that's a trend that continues through the series. Overall, I'd say Mr. Brooks is off to a fine start as far as I'm concerned. The only thing that kept this from getting a five-star rating was the way the pacing took its sweet time in a few places. Other than that, I can't complain!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2549742902551136960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_38495819" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38495819" />
    <a title="Jenni" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1744181-jenni"><img alt="Jenni" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1227491101p2/1744181.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38495819?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenni" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenni" href="/user/show/1744181-jenni">Jenni</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38495819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4556856502730598328">I love fantasy books, so of course Terry Brooks was on my list of must reads. The Landover series books were great for many reasons. First it was a light read. I am not saying there is no moral dilemas or complexity, just that you dont have to wrap your brain too deeply around it. I also liked it for the entertainment factor. There was action, but not too much, love interests, but not too much, magic... well you can't overdo that in a fantasy book, evil villians, a bumbling wizard (every fantasy</span>
  <span id="freeText4556856502730598328" style="display:none">I love fantasy books, so of course Terry Brooks was on my list of must reads. The Landover series books were great for many reasons. First it was a light read. I am not saying there is no moral dilemas or complexity, just that you dont have to wrap your brain too deeply around it. I also liked it for the entertainment factor. There was action, but not too much, love interests, but not too much, magic... well you can't overdo that in a fantasy book, evil villians, a bumbling wizard (every fantasy book needs one, right?), and of course a underdog that discovers himself to be the hero. I just thought it was the right kind of book to sit back and relax and read in a day. Plus it has the added benefit of having 4 more books to read afterwards. I'd recomend it for when you want to read a fantasy book but arent in the mood to see half the characters die or try to figure out the movements of a sword in a fight or armys in a war, or contimplate the inplications of harnessing magical power. If you are looking for that then read his shannara series instead.</span>

  <span id="freeText11631413528450558525" style="display:none">A really interesting story with a good premise, but could have been filled out a bit better and expanded upon to give a richer feel for the land, the people and the events. The message of fear being one's worst enemy and defeating you before you even start was a good one and because of this I got a lot out of the book, but I felt that events and descriptions were far too sparse and that this was the abridged version, though I know it wasn't. <span id="freeTextContainer5334569696380005300">Re: _Magic Kingdom for Sale--Sold" by Terry Brooks <br/><br/>This is part of Brooks' Magic Kingdom of Landover series. This book is the series opener. My GR friend, Werner says: "With this series, there is a case for reading the books in order; the first one gives some essential basic information, and there is a progressive development of the characters...".<br/><br/>I enjoyed reading this book of fantasy. It kept me reading. It was easy to follow and the fantasy characters were fun to read about. There's suspense </span>
  <span id="freeText5334569696380005300" style="display:none">Re: _Magic Kingdom for Sale--Sold" by Terry Brooks <br /><br />This is part of Brooks' Magic Kingdom of Landover series. This book is the series opener. My GR friend, Werner says: "With this series, there is a case for reading the books in order; the first one gives some essential basic information, and there is a progressive development of the characters...".<br /><br />I enjoyed reading this book of fantasy. It kept me reading. It was easy to follow and the fantasy characters were fun to read about. There's suspense and some humor. This is a wonderfully imaginative book to cozy-up and relax with for easy entertainment.<br /><br />Surprisingly, I picked up some lessons for life from this book. There's a sub-text in which the author demonstrates, through his main character, Ben Holiday, how to overcome fear and how to maintain determination in the face of almost impossible circumstances. Interesting how a simple story like this can deliver such huge lessons subtly and effectively (without preaching), thanks to the skill of its author. Terry Brooks has created a very likable character in Ben Holiday, who sets out against great odds to become King of Landover.<br /><br />Now I look forward to the next books in the Landover series:<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/92845.The_Black_Unicorn__Magic_Kingdom_of_Landover___2_" title="The Black Unicorn (Magic Kingdom of Landover, #2) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">The Black Unicorn</a> (Magic Kingdom of Landover, #2)<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15561.Wizard_at_Large__Magic_Kingdom_of_Landover___3_" title="Wizard at Large (Magic Kingdom of Landover, #3) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Wizard at Large</a> (Magic Kingdom of Landover, #3)</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1431922236" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1431922236" />
    <a title="Kelsey Hanson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14303907-kelsey-hanson"><img alt="Kelsey Hanson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353034986p2/14303907.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1431922236?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelsey Hanson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelsey Hanson" href="/user/show/14303907-kelsey-hanson">Kelsey Hanson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14303907-kelsey-hanson?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14303907-kelsey-hanson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1431922236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6515879937869326320">Back in the early 2000s when I first discovered Terry Brooks, I read this series mainly as a way to pass the time when I read out of "Shannara" books. Now rereading this, I appreciate it much more now. I think it is perhaps as an adult, I better appreciate Ben's world weariness and the thought of "What would you do if you had the chance to rule a country and essentially create your own government". This book is also very fun and imaginative with a snarky main character. I also really like the g'</span>
  <span id="freeText6515879937869326320" style="display:none">Back in the early 2000s when I first discovered Terry Brooks, I read this series mainly as a way to pass the time when I read out of "Shannara" books. Now rereading this, I appreciate it much more now. I think it is perhaps as an adult, I better appreciate Ben's world weariness and the thought of "What would you do if you had the chance to rule a country and essentially create your own government". This book is also very fun and imaginative with a snarky main character. I also really like the g'home gnomes. They definitely amuse me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6515879937869326320" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_310273586" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/310273586" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1353392-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521752891p2/1353392.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/310273586?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/1353392-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer310273586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4095954853022780970">Ben Holiday, attorney at law, is dissatisfied with his life. He sees the justice system becoming more and more flawed and his profession become the butt of every bad lawyer joke. His wife has passed away and he is increasingly withdrawn. When he sees an advertisement for a honest-to-goodness magic kingdom in the Christmas Wishbook, he seizes on his chance to give some more meaning and purpose to his life. He's got more than he bargained for when he arrives to find the kingdom in disrepair and no</span>
  <span id="freeText4095954853022780970" style="display:none">Ben Holiday, attorney at law, is dissatisfied with his life. He sees the justice system becoming more and more flawed and his profession become the butt of every bad lawyer joke. His wife has passed away and he is increasingly withdrawn. When he sees an advertisement for a honest-to-goodness magic kingdom in the Christmas Wishbook, he seizes on his chance to give some more meaning and purpose to his life. He's got more than he bargained for when he arrives to find the kingdom in disrepair and no small amount of dangerous foes clamoring for his throne and his only allies a talking dog, an inept wizard, two kobolds and a girl who is part tree. <br />With such a premise, I expected this book to be much funnier than it was. I was only disappointed for a few minutes, though, because the story was so engaging as it was. I am not a huge fan of swords and magic epic fantasy, but this really brought a new twist, what with the protagonist being so out of place within the fantasy world. He spends just the right amount of time being amazed and disbelieving of his situation before coming to terms with the reality of the magic and the danger. He shows a lot of fortitude, but not so much that it comes across as disingenuous. The dynamism of the character is also an asset to the narrative. His rag-tag band of supporters are also able to learn and grow through their experiences with Ben, but not so much that there is no room for further development in the sequels, of which there are several. The climax and resolution of the tale is also just the right amount of satisfying whiles still leaving threads to be followed up with in later books. <br />I must also say that I listened to an audio book of the author's seminal work, <i>The Sword of Shannara</i>, some years ago, and despite the fact that it was the Absolute Favorite Book Ever of the guy I was seeing at the time, was not wholly enamored of the tale. I felt it went on too long and that it did not seem terribly original or engaging. Of course I was also driving from Minnesota to Georgia at the time and might have missed some things while my attention was diverted by traffic. I am pleased to say that I found this book much more pleasurable and may be induced to give that other series a try at some point. I continue to be told that it is rather good. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4095954853022780970" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_97281734" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97281734" />
    <a title="Robert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2278428-robert"><img alt="Robert" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1241268476p2/2278428.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97281734?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert" href="/user/show/2278428-robert">Robert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278428-robert?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97281734" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17871459836607176743">It sounds like the premise of a hilarious comic fantasy: Successful lawyer sees a magic kingdom for sale in a Christmas catalogue, buys it, and becomes king. Except, things are not as grand as they seem, and he finds himself accompanied by a talking dog, an incompetent wizard, and two goblins as his only retinue...<br/><br/>Unfortunately, the book never really delivers anything at all. The writing is bland, the humour is, for the most part, absent, and the story is altogether a misfire. There is a touch o</span>
  <span id="freeText17871459836607176743" style="display:none">It sounds like the premise of a hilarious comic fantasy: Successful lawyer sees a magic kingdom for sale in a Christmas catalogue, buys it, and becomes king. Except, things are not as grand as they seem, and he finds himself accompanied by a talking dog, an incompetent wizard, and two goblins as his only retinue...<br /><br />Unfortunately, the book never really delivers anything at all. The writing is bland, the humour is, for the most part, absent, and the story is altogether a misfire. There is a touch of fairy tale magic in some plot elements, but it is never delivered in an engaging or delightful way. A saucy minx bathing naked in a lake? Check. A last dragon? Check. A canny evil witch? Check. Do any of them manage to add any energy to the story? Fail.<br /><br />Our hero is a rich lawyer who has lost his wife and still hasn't overcome her loss. He's frustrated with his profession, grumpy, and looking for something to take his mind of things, and a challenge. Enter the magic kingdom sale. Perhaps if our hero wasn't so busy telling us every emotion he felt, he might be more interesting. Perhaps if he didn't yoyo between cocky lawyer confidence and self-berating failure so frequently, he might be less tedious. But everything about Ben Holiday is tedious. Everything about the kingdom is unfulfilling, not magical enough, a world fallen flat.<br /><br />So, on the whole, a book that did not make me want to read the other two in this series, or pick up any other Terry Brooks book. I once played a PC game about Shannarah. It was fun. This book, sadly, wasn't, and I am not sure I see the merits in his writing. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17871459836607176743" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_76421218" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/76421218" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/76421218?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345317582" href="/book/show/17721.Magic_Kingdom_for_Sale_Sold_">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=multi-dimensional">multi-dimensional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=romance-y">romance-y</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer76421218" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9931883084989810100">This was definitely a fun and easy read. Ben Holiday is a disenchanted lawyer who is trying to find some purpose to his life after his wife and unborn child died in a tragic accident. When he sees an advertisement for a magic kingdom being sold for $1 Million, he all but jumps at the chance, even though he only partially believes it could be real. <br/><br/>Of course it is, and there is everything promised in the ad -- except not quite exactly as promised. Everything is running down and withering, because</span>
  <span id="freeText9931883084989810100" style="display:none">This was definitely a fun and easy read. Ben Holiday is a disenchanted lawyer who is trying to find some purpose to his life after his wife and unborn child died in a tragic accident. When he sees an advertisement for a magic kingdom being sold for $1 Million, he all but jumps at the chance, even though he only partially believes it could be real. <br /><br />Of course it is, and there is everything promised in the ad -- except not quite exactly as promised. Everything is running down and withering, because the magic is running out. His magic kingdom is dying and needs a King to save it. <br /><br />A bit of a problem there though, as none of the inhabitants in the land have much faith in a king who's bought his kingship... Not a heck of a lot you can do as King with only 4 loyal subjects. <br /><br />This was my very first Brooks book, and I have to say that Brooks' writing style, especially the action sequences, is great. I felt like I was there, that I knew what was going on and how everyone felt about it. During some of the more tense moments, I was literally on edge waiting for the outcome. Things never really resolved themselves in the way I'd have expected, and I like that too. I like being kept on my toes!<br /><br />Very nice story, well-written and interesting. Not at all what I was expecting. I will definitely be on the look-out for the rest of the series. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9931883084989810100" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_50880951" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/50880951" />
    <a title="Debbie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1185055-debbie"><img alt="Debbie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316211185p2/1185055.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/50880951?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie" href="/user/show/1185055-debbie">Debbie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345317582" href="/book/show/17721.Magic_Kingdom_for_Sale_Sold_">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer50880951&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50880951" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15977841522509294764">Listening to this book was so enjoyable. Dick Hill performed the narration and did an excellent job - as he usually does. The story itself was rather more relevant to today than I expected for a book written in 1986. The main character Ben is a disillusioned, depressed lawyer who can't move on after his wife is killed in a accident. He answers an ad in an exclusive wish book catalog about buying a kingdom with all the trimmings; dragons, fairies, wizards, etc. <br/><br/>Trouble starts before Ben even gets</span>
  <span id="freeText15977841522509294764" style="display:none">Listening to this book was so enjoyable. Dick Hill performed the narration and did an excellent job - as he usually does. The story itself was rather more relevant to today than I expected for a book written in 1986. The main character Ben is a disillusioned, depressed lawyer who can't move on after his wife is killed in a accident. He answers an ad in an exclusive wish book catalog about buying a kingdom with all the trimmings; dragons, fairies, wizards, etc. <br /><br />Trouble starts before Ben even gets to his kingdom, and is compounded each day by new problems. It seems the magic that holds the kingdom together is fading since there has been no king on the throne for 20 some years. As Ben meets each new challenge from the kingdom he overcomes challenges from himself as well. He learns new things about himself and his motives that eventually lead to his victory in saving the kingdom (this is a story about magic, after all). At the end of the book as he stands before his subjects outlining his plans for restoring the kingdom to its former glory, I couldn't help but hear echoes of President Obama's speeches in my mind. Ben is tackling pollution, disparate trade systems, isolationism, and lost hopes. It just sounds too familiar. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15977841522509294764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1089546715339291446" style="display:none">Thank you to my papa for the recommendation!<br /><br />I enjoyed this, the ending was excellent!<br />I had a little issue with the beginning, if I've agreed to suspend disbelief, I don't need 70 pages of Ben trying to convince himself or talking of the silliness or impossibility or whatever. This is not a bad thing, as obviously this other world needs explaining, it is like nothing we have other seen, but there were times when the length of the descriptions interfered with the momentum of the story--for me anyway.<br /><br />I loved the characters, the relate-ability of them, their loyalty. I am looking forward to continuing the series.</span>

<div id="review_2718511290" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2718511290" />
    <a title="Akshaya Sriram" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32658828-akshaya-sriram"><img alt="Akshaya Sriram" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513129640p2/32658828.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2718511290?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Akshaya Sriram" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Akshaya Sriram" href="/user/show/32658828-akshaya-sriram">Akshaya Sriram</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2718511290" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14085370951751143360">Terry Brooks has built a world of magic and chaos that is as fantastic as Wonderland in this book: Ben Holiday tries to get away from personal tragedy by buying and becoming king of a magical place called Landover. It his adventures in Landover that make the tale. Brooks has built a world that is definitely magical with a very fairy tale air to it. The characters: Questor Thews, the wizard who casts spells that isn't 'just right' and Abernathy, the dog-advisor who is constantly displeased, the g</span>
  <span id="freeText14085370951751143360" style="display:none">Terry Brooks has built a world of magic and chaos that is as fantastic as Wonderland in this book: Ben Holiday tries to get away from personal tragedy by buying and becoming king of a magical place called Landover. It his adventures in Landover that make the tale. Brooks has built a world that is definitely magical with a very fairy tale air to it. The characters: Questor Thews, the wizard who casts spells that isn't 'just right' and Abernathy, the dog-advisor who is constantly displeased, the gnomes who're akin to tweedle dum and tweedle dee are hilarious additions to this story. <br />But where he excels at descriptive imagery, he fails at building character relationship and pace. The romance did not take very well to Ben Holiday, widower who still mourns his wife and the pace was so slow, i plodded along to finish the book. Yes Landover has its flaws, but it also has a strong foundation in a new world and solid characters. <br />3 Bonnie Blue stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14085370951751143360" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3541248214" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3541248214" />
    <a title="Steve R" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51602729-steve-r"><img alt="Steve R" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550608435p2/51602729.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3541248214?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steve R" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steve R" href="/user/show/51602729-steve-r">Steve R</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3541248214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16096472332483564407">This 1986 fantasy novel was the first in a series of seven books making up The Magic Kingdom of Landover series. I found them as a whole a vast improvement over Brooks' Shannara series, which seemed to be excessively bogged down in a repetititve manner of plot construction. On the other hand, the Landover books presented something much lighter, often quite humorous, and nowhere near as predictable an experience. It is as if Brooks suddenly remembered that reading should be a fun activity for the</span>
  <span id="freeText16096472332483564407" style="display:none">This 1986 fantasy novel was the first in a series of seven books making up The Magic Kingdom of Landover series. I found them as a whole a vast improvement over Brooks' Shannara series, which seemed to be excessively bogged down in a repetititve manner of plot construction. On the other hand, the Landover books presented something much lighter, often quite humorous, and nowhere near as predictable an experience. It is as if Brooks suddenly remembered that reading should be a fun activity for the reader as much as it should be as suspenseful one.<br /><br />Good stuff.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16096472332483564407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_201722064" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/201722064" />
    <a title="Lanica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1336787-lanica"><img alt="Lanica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1217471726p2/1336787.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/201722064?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lanica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lanica" href="/user/show/1336787-lanica">Lanica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1336787-lanica?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1336787-lanica?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer201722064" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7966988372487785157">PERSONAL REVIEW:<br/>I was pretty unimpressed...but I think it's just not my type of book. I never got into Douglas Adams or Monty Python either. I wonder if a lot of the humor just went right over my head...it was too dry, or to wet, or something...anyhow, although I could see where the humor was, I just wasn't finding it funny. <br/><br/>Additionally, story alone was pretty dull stuff. A man buys a kingdom...it's not what he expected...he goes from person to person asking for help and then it all ties nicely</span>
  <span id="freeText7966988372487785157" style="display:none">PERSONAL REVIEW:<br />I was pretty unimpressed...but I think it's just not my type of book. I never got into Douglas Adams or Monty Python either. I wonder if a lot of the humor just went right over my head...it was too dry, or to wet, or something...anyhow, although I could see where the humor was, I just wasn't finding it funny. <br /><br />Additionally, story alone was pretty dull stuff. A man buys a kingdom...it's not what he expected...he goes from person to person asking for help and then it all ties nicely together in the end. A simplistic conclusion for a simple book. <br /><br />I expected more, but I suppose I should have looked at the juvenile males who were exhorting it's virtues and aligned my expectation with their idea of 'good' instead of mine. That's one of the dangers of working in a middle school, I guess.<br /><br />MIDDLE SCHOOL LIBRARIAN REVIEW:<br />Boys in my library love this book, so I had to read it. Anything that gets boys reading gets a star bump just for having been written. Although I didn't enjoy the humor, a lot of my students have told me that they laughed out loud at this book. I think I'll have to ask them which parts those were. :) It's a long book for most kids, so I am continually impressed that they finish it. It has a main character that is not a teen - so what do they find to connect with? I guess it's just the adventure. This book reads like a D&amp;D module: simple plot, tightly tied band of characters, a strange mix of creatures...what's not to love if you're a boy?<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7966988372487785157" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1699032042" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1699032042" />
    <a title="Al Philipson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4519287-al-philipson"><img alt="Al Philipson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442518914p2/4519287.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1699032042?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Al Philipson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Al Philipson" href="/user/show/4519287-al-philipson">Al Philipson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1699032042" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13643696786034562566">Brooks' writing is superb. It flows well and doesn't distract from the story itself. I felt that I was there, struggling along with Ben (the main character).<br/><br/>The story line itself was decent and worth an occasional re-read (this is my second time). For me, it was slow in a couple of places and a bit frustrating (possibly because Ben was having TOO much trouble securing his throne?). I'll probably read it again in a few years if I'm still processing oxygen.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kD2S2xm5bitgZ+BUxytK1PZNw1KUlIyx0pkOzAetKNW1reHmAzAUMnxvgJd1kCLCjxkdtXyUEwauQEhwGPdFfA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Le80RrRTdgxy04T8Z4B3Mxt6K3iGFD/SgywQi9CARCcIf0d7rtoMFW7b5D/VOx8lYi71n24UoGX/9VY3z9opjg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17419096640108175943">Terry Brooks was born in Illinois in 1944, where he spent a great deal of his childhood and early adulthood dreaming up stories in and around Sinnissippi Park, the very same park that would eventually become the setting for his bestselling Word & Void trilogy. He went to college and received his undergraduate degree from Hamilton College, where he majored in English Literature, and he received his</span>
  <span id="freeText17419096640108175943" style="display:none">Terry Brooks was born in Illinois in 1944, where he spent a great deal of his childhood and early adulthood dreaming up stories in and around Sinnissippi Park, the very same park that would eventually become the setting for his bestselling Word &amp; Void trilogy. He went to college and received his undergraduate degree from Hamilton College, where he majored in English Literature, and he received his graduate degree from the School of Law at Washington &amp; Lee University.<br />A writer since high school, he wrote many stories within the genres of science fiction, western, fiction, and non-fiction, until one semester early in his college years he was given The Lord of the Rings to read. That moment changed Terry's life forever, because in Tolkien's great work he found all the elements needed to fully explore his writing combined in one genre.<br />He then wrote The Sword of Shannara, the seven year grand result retaining sanity while studying at Washington &amp; Lee University and practicing law. It became the first work of fiction ever to appear on the New York Times trade paperback bestseller list, where it remained for over five months.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17419096640108175943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]>
</script>
